Think of it like a toolbox with ready-to-use tools.\n\n#### OpenAI's AI Models\nThese are advanced machine learning models developed by OpenAI that can understand and generate human-like text based on the input they receive. They're like very smart robots that can talk, write, and even help with coding.\n\n#### SDK (Software Development Kit)\nA collection of software tools and libraries designed to help developers create applications for specific platforms. Think of it like a starter kit with everything you need to build something.\n\n#### API (Application Programming Interface)\nA set of rules that lets different software programs communicate with each other. It's like a menu in a restaurant where you can see what you can order, how to order it, and what you get in return.\n\n#### HTTP (HyperText Transfer Protocol)\nA protocol used for transferring data over the web. It's like the language that computers use to talk to each other on the internet.\n\n#### HTTPS (HyperText Transfer Protocol Secure)\nThe secure version of HTTP. It means the data transferred is encrypted and secure, like sending a locked package instead of a postcard.\n\n#### Request\nWhen you ask a computer to do something or get some data. It's like placing an order online.\n\n#### Proxy\nA server that acts as an intermediary between your computer and the internet. It can help with security, anonymity, and speeding up access to resources.\n\n#### Streaming Responses\nGetting parts of a response as they come in, rather than waiting for the whole response. It's like watching a YouTube video as it loads instead of downloading the entire video first.\n\n#### Asynchronous\nDoing multiple things at the same time without waiting for each task to complete one by one. It's like cooking several dishes at once instead of one after the other.\n\n#### Parameters\nPieces of information you provide to a function or request to control how it works. It's like giving specific instructions when you order food, like \"no onions.\"\n\n#### Nested Parameters\nParameters that are inside other parameters, like a list inside a list. It's like a folder within a folder on your computer.\n\n#### Fine-Tuning Models\nCustomizing an AI model with additional training to improve its performance for specific tasks. It's like teaching a robot to do a new trick.\n\n#### Error Handling\nWays to manage and respond to errors that occur in your program. It's like having a plan for what to do if something goes wrong.\n\n#### Endpoints\nSpecific addresses where APIs can access resources or perform actions. It's like the different sections of a website you can visit.\n\n#### AzureOpenAI\nA version of OpenAI that works with Microsoft Azure, a cloud computing service. It's like using OpenAI's tools through Microsoft's platform.\n\n#### Python\nA popular programming language known for its simplicity and readability. It's great for beginners and experts alike.\n\n#### Stainless\nA tool used to generate this library from the OpenAPI specification. It's like a machine that builds software tools based on detailed blueprints.\n\n---\n\nI hope this revised section meets your needs! The [library](#library) includes type definitions for all request [params](#parameters) and response fields, and offers both synchronous and [asynchronous](#asynchronous) clients powered by [httpx](#http).\n\nIt is generated from our [OpenAPI](#api) specification with [Stainless](#stainless).\n\n---\n\n **Explanation:**\nThe OpenAI Python library is like a toolbox that makes it easy to use OpenAI's AI models in your Python programs. Imagine you have a smart robot assistant that can help you with various tasks like answering questions or generating text. This library helps you communicate with that robot using a set of rules (API) over the internet.\n\n---\n\n\u003cdetails\u003e\n\u003csummary\u003e\u003cb\u003eTable of Contents\u003c/b\u003e\u003c/summary\u003e\n\n- [Documentation](#documentation)\n- [Installation](#installation)\n- [Usage](#usage)\n- [Polling Helpers](#polling-helpers)\n- [Bulk Upload Helpers](#bulk-upload-helpers)\n- [Streaming Helpers](#streaming-helpers)\n- [Async Usage](#async-usage)\n- [Streaming Responses](#streaming-responses)\n- [Module-Level Client](#module-level-client)\n- [Using Types](#using-types)\n- [Pagination](#pagination)\n- [Nested Params](#nested-params)\n- [File Uploads](#file-uploads)\n- [Handling Errors](#handling-errors)\n- [Retries](#retries)\n- [Timeouts](#timeouts)\n- [Advanced](#advanced)\n  - [Logging](#logging)\n  - [Making Custom/Undocumented Requests](#making-custom-undocumented-requests)\n  - [Configuring the HTTP Client](#configuring-the-http-client)\n  - [Managing HTTP Resources](#managing-http-resources)\n- [Microsoft Azure OpenAI](#microsoft-azure-openai)\n- [Requirements](#requirements)\n- [Versioning](#versioning)\n\n\u003c/details\u003e\n\n---\n\n## Documentation\n\nThe [REST API](#rest-api) documentation can be found on [platform.openai.com](https://platform.openai.com/docs). The full API of this [library](#library) can be found in [api.md](api.md).\n\n---\n\n **Explanation:**\nThe OpenAI documentation is like a user manual for this system. It has all the instructions and information you need to use OpenAI's AI models in your Python programs. Think of it as a detailed guide that shows you how to communicate with your smart robot assistant.\n\n---\n\n## Installation\n\n\u003e [!IMPORTANT]\n\u003e The [SDK](#sdk) was rewritten in v1, which was released November 6th 2023. See the [v1 migration guide](https://github.com/openai/openai-python/discussions/742), which includes scripts to automatically update your code.\n\n```sh\n# install from PyPI\npip install openai\n```\n\n---\n\n **Explanation:**\nTo use this library, you need to install it first. This is like installing a new app on your phone, but for Python. Imagine you are adding a new tool to your toolbox so you can use it in your programming projects.\n\n**Example:**\n\n```sh\npip install openai\n```\n\nThe OpenAI is the company who created this system, and the library is like a book shop with different packages like books, that you can use in your Python scripts. For example, `import openai` connects your script to the library for commands and instructions.\n\n---\n\n## Usage\n\nThe full API of this library can be found in [api.md](api.md).\n\n```python\nimport os\nfrom openai import OpenAI\n\nclient = OpenAI(\n    api_key=os.environ.get(\"OPENAI_API_KEY\"),\n)\n\nchat_completion = client.chat.completions.create(\n    messages=[\n        {\n            \"role\": \"user\",\n            \"content\": \"Say this is a test\",\n        }\n    ],\n    model=\"gpt-3.5-turbo\",\n)\n```\n\n---\n\n **Explanation:**\nHere's how you use the library to talk to the AI models. Think of this like having a conversation with your smart robot assistant. You set up the connection, ask it to say something, and then it responds.\n\n**Example:**\n\n```python\nimport os\nfrom openai import OpenAI\n\nclient = OpenAI(api_key=os.environ.get(\"OPENAI_API_KEY\"))\n\nchat_completion = client.chat.completions.create(\n    model=\"gpt-3.5-turbo\",\n    messages=[{\"role\": \"user\", \"content\": \"Say this is a test\"}],\n)\n\nprint(chat_completion.choices[0].message.content)\n```\n\nThis code sets up the AI client and asks it to say \"This is a test.\"\n\n---\n\n## Polling Helpers\n\nWhen interacting with the API some actions such as starting a Run and adding files to vector stores are asynchronous and take time to complete. The SDK includes helper functions which will poll the status until it reaches a terminal state and then return the resulting object. If an API method results in an action that could benefit from polling there will be a corresponding version of the method ending in '\\_and_poll'.\n\nFor instance to create a Run and poll until it reaches a terminal state you can run:\n\n```python\nrun = client.beta.threads.runs.create_and_poll(\n    thread_id=thread.id,\n    assistant_id=assistant.id,\n)\n```\n\n---\n\n **Explanation:**\nSome actions take time to complete, like starting a process or uploading files. Polling helpers keep checking until these actions are done. Imagine you are baking a cake and you keep checking the oven until the cake is ready.\n\n**Example:**\n\n```python\nrun = client.beta.threads.runs.create_and_poll(\n    thread_id=thread.id,\n    assistant_id=assistant.id,\n)\n```\n\nThis code starts a process and waits until it's finished.\n\n---\n\n## Bulk Upload Helpers\n\nWhen creating and interacting with vector stores, you can use polling helpers to monitor the status of operations. For convenience, we also provide a bulk upload helper to allow you to simultaneously upload several files at once.\n\n```python\nsample_files = [Path(\"sample-paper.pdf\"), ...]\n\nbatch = await client.vector_stores.file_batches.upload_and_poll(\n    store.id,\n    files=sample_files,\n)\n```\n\n---\n\n **Explanation:**\nYou can upload multiple files at once and check their status. This is like sending a bunch of letters at the post office and waiting to see when they are all delivered.\n\n**Example:**\n\n```python\nfrom pathlib import Path\n\nsample_files = [Path(\"sample-paper.pdf\"), ...]\n\nbatch = await client.vector_stores.file_batches.upload_and_poll(\n    store.id,\n    files=sample_files,\n)\n```\n\nThis code uploads several files and waits until they're all done.\n\n---\n\n## Streaming Helpers\n\nThe SDK also includes helpers to process streams and handle incoming events.\n\n```python\nwith client.beta.threads.runs.stream(\n    thread_id=thread.id,\n    assistant_id=assistant.id,\n    instructions=\"Please address the user as Jane Doe. The user has a premium account.\",\n) as stream:\n    for event in stream:\n        if event.type == \"thread.message.delta\" and event.data.delta.content:\n            print(event.data.delta.content[0].text)\n```\n\n---\n\n **Explanation:**\nYou can stream responses from the AI, which means you get parts of the response as they come in, instead of waiting for the whole thing. It's like watching a YouTube video as it loads rather than waiting for the entire video to download first.\n\n**Example:**\n\n```python\nwith client.beta.threads.runs.stream(\n    thread_id=thread.id,\n    assistant_id=assistant.id,\n    instructions=\"Please address the user as Jane Doe. The user has a premium account.\",\n) as stream:\n    for event in stream:\n        if event.type == \"thread.message.delta\" and event.data.delta.content:\n            print(event.data.delta.content[0].text)\n```\n\nThis code streams the response from the AI and prints it piece by piece.\n\n---\n\n## Async Usage\n\nSimply import `AsyncOpenAI` instead of `OpenAI` and use `await` with each API call:\n\n```python\nimport os\nimport asyncio\nfrom openai import AsyncOpenAI\n\nclient = AsyncOpenAI(\n    api_key=os.environ.get(\"OPENAI_API_KEY\"),\n)\n\nasync def main() -\u003e None:\n    chat_completion = await client.chat.completions.create(\n        messages=[\n            {\n                \"role\": \"user\",\n                \"content\": \"Say this is a test\",\n            }\n        ],\n        model=\"gpt-3.5-turbo\",\n    )\n\nasyncio.run(main())\n```\n\nFunctionality between the synchronous and asynchronous clients is otherwise identical.\n\n---\n\n **Explanation:**\nYou can use the library with asynchronous code, which lets your program do other things while waiting for the AI to respond. It's like cooking several dishes at once instead of one after the other.\n\n**Example:**\n\n```python\nimport os\nimport asyncio\nfrom openai import AsyncOpenAI\n\nclient = AsyncOpenAI(api_key=os.environ.get(\"OPENAI_API_KEY\"))\n\nasync def main() -\u003e None:\n    chat_completion = await client.chat.completions.create(\n        model=\"gpt-3.5-turbo\",\n        messages=[{\"role\": \"user\", \"content\": \"Say this is a test\"}],\n import OpenAI\n\nclient = OpenAI()\n\nstream = client.chat.completions.create(\n    model=\"gpt-4\",\n    messages=[{\"role\": \"user\", \"content\": \"Say this is a test\"}],\n    stream=True,\n)\nfor chunk in stream:\n    print(chunk.choices[0].delta.content or \"\", end=\"\")\n```\n\nThe async client uses the exact same interface.\n\n```python\nfrom openai import AsyncOpenAI\n\nclient = AsyncOpenAI()\n\nasync def main():\n    stream = await client.chat.completions.create(\n        model=\"gpt-4\",\n        messages=[{\"role\": \"user\", \"content\": \"Say this is a test\"}],\n        stream=True,\n    )\n    async for chunk in stream:\n        print(chunk.choices[0].delta.content or \"\", end=\"\")\n\nasyncio.run(main())\n```\n\n---\n\n **Explanation:**\nYou can handle streaming responses from the AI in both synchronous and asynchronous ways. It's like watching a live broadcast or listening to live radio where the content comes in chunks.\n\n**Example:**\n\n```python\nfrom openai import OpenAI\n\nclient = OpenAI()\n\nstream = client.chat.completions.create(\n    model=\"gpt-4\",\n    messages=[{\"role\": \"user\", \"content\": \"Say this is a test\"}],\n    stream=True,\n)\nfor chunk in stream:\n    print(chunk.choices[0].delta.content or \"\", end=\"\")\n```\n\nThis code streams the response from the AI and prints it as it comes.\n\n---\n\n## Module-Level Client\n\nYou can set up a global client instance, which is useful for quick experiments but not recommended for complex applications.\n\n```py\nimport openai\n\nopenai.api_key = 'your-api-key'\n\ncompletion = openai.chat.completions.create(\n    model=\"gpt-4\",\n    messages=[{\"role\": \"user\", \"content\": \"How do I output all files in a directory using Python?\"}],\n)\n\nprint(completion.choices[0].message.content)\n```\n\n---\n\n **Explanation:**\nYou can set up a global client instance, which is useful for quick experiments but not recommended for complex applications. It's like having a universal remote that works for all your devices, but it might not have all the features you need for each specific device.\n\n**Example:**\n\n```python\nimport openai\n\nopenai.api_key = 'your-api-key'\n\ncompletion = openai.chat.completions.create(\n    model=\"gpt-4\",\n    messages=[{\"role\": \"user\", \"content\": \"How do I output all files in a directory using Python?\"}],\n)\n\nprint(completion.choices[0].message.content)\n```\n\nThis code uses a global client to get a response from the AI.\n\n---\n\n## Using Types\n\nThe library uses typed requests and responses, which means it can help you catch mistakes while you write your code.\n\n```python\nfrom openai import OpenAI\n\nclient = OpenAI()\n\ncompletion = client.chat.completions.create(\n    messages=[{\"role\": \"user\", \"content\": \"Can you generate an example json object describing a fruit?\"}],\n    model=\"gpt-3.5-turbo-1106\",\n    response_format={\"type\": \"json_object\"},\n)\n```\n\n---\n\n **Explanation:**\nThe library uses typed requests and responses, which means it can help you catch mistakes while you write your code. Think of it as having a spell-checker for your programming instructions.\n\n**Example:**\n\n```python\nfrom openai import OpenAI\n\nclient = OpenAI()\n\ncompletion = client.chat.completions.create(\n    messages=[{\"role\": \"user\", \"content\": \"Can you generate an example json object describing a fruit?\"}],\n    model=\"gpt-3.5-turbo-1106\",\n    response_format={\"type\": \"json_object\"},\n)\n```\n\nThis code asks the AI to generate a JSON object describing a fruit.\n\n---\n\n## Pagination\n\nSome API responses are too large to send all at once, so they are split into pages. The library can automatically handle fetching these pages for you.\n\n```python\nimport openai\n\nclient = OpenAI()\n\nall_jobs = []\nfor job in client.fine_tuning.jobs.list(limit=20):\n    all_jobs.append(job)\n\nprint(all_jobs)\n```\n\n---\n\n **Explanation:**\nSome API responses are too large to send all at once, so they are split into pages. The library can automatically handle fetching these pages for you. It's like getting a long book in several smaller, manageable volumes instead of one big, heavy book.\n\n**Example:**\n\n```python\nimport openai\n\nclient = OpenAI()\n\nall_jobs = []\nfor job in client.fine_tuning.jobs.list(limit=20):\n    all_jobs.append(job)\n\nprint(all_jobs)\n```\n\nThis code fetches all jobs, automatically handling multiple pages of results.\n\n---\n\n## Nested Params\n\nSome parameters are nested dictionaries. You can pass them as dictionaries in your requests.\n\n```python\nfrom openai import OpenAI\n\nclient = OpenAI()\n\ncompletion = client.chat.completions.create(\n    messages=[{\"role\": \"user\", \"content\": \"Can you generate an example json object describing a fruit?\"}],\n    model=\"gpt-3.5-turbo-1106\",\n    response_format={\"type\": \"json_object\"},\n)\n```\n\n---\n\n **Explanation:**\nSome parameters are nested dictionaries. You can pass them as dictionaries in your requests. It's like having a folder inside another folder on your computer.\n\n**Example:**\n\n```python\nfrom openai import OpenAI\n\nclient = OpenAI()\n\ncompletion = client.chat.completions.create(\n    messages=[{\"role\": \"user\", \"content\": \"Can you generate an example json object describing a fruit?\"}],\n    model=\"gpt-3.5-turbo-1106\",\n    response_format={\"type\": \"json_object\"},\n)\n```\n\nThis code asks the AI to generate a JSON object.\n\n---\n\n## File Uploads\n\nYou can upload files directly to the API, which can be used for things like fine-tuning models.\n\n```python\nfrom pathlib import Path\nfrom openai import OpenAI\n\nclient = OpenAI()\n\nclient.files.create(\n    file=Path(\"input.jsonl\"),\n    purpose=\"fine-tune\",\n)\n```\n\n---\n\n **Explanation:**\nYou can upload files directly to the API, which can be used for things like fine-tuning models. It's like uploading a document to a website so that the site can use the information in the document.\n\n**Example:**\n\n```python\nfrom pathlib import Path\nfrom openai import OpenAI\n\nclient = OpenAI()\n\nclient.files.create(\n    file=Path(\"input.jsonl\"),\n    purpose=\"fine-tune\",\n)\n```\n\nThis code uploads a file for fine-tuning a model.\n\n---\n\n## Handling Errors\n\nThe library provides error handling for different types of errors that can occur while interacting with the API.\n\n```python\nimport openai\nfrom openai import OpenAI\n\nclient = OpenAI()\n\ntry:\n    client.fine_tuning.jobs.create(\n        model=\"gpt-3.5-turbo\",\n        training_file=\"file-abc123\",\n    )\nexcept openai.APIConnectionError as e:\n    print(\"The server could not be reached\")\n    print(e.__cause__)\nexcept openai.RateLimitError as e:\n    print(\"A 429 status code was received; we should back off a bit.\")\nexcept openai.APIStatusError as e:\n    print(\"Another non-200-range status code was received\")\n    print(e.status_code)\n    print(e.response)\n```\n\n---\n\n **Explanation:**\nThe library provides error handling for different types of errors that can occur while interacting with the API. It's like having a plan for what to do if something goes wrong while you're working on a project.\n\n**Example:**\n\n```python\nimport openai\nfrom openai import OpenAI\n\nclient = OpenAI()\n\ntry:\n    client.fine_tuning.jobs.create(\n        model=\"gpt-3.5-turbo\",\n        training_file=\"file-abc123\",\n    )\nexcept openai.APIConnectionError as e:\n    print(\"The server could not be reached\")\n    print(e.__cause__)\nexcept openai.RateLimitError as e:\n    print(\"A 429 status code was received; we should back off a bit.\")\nexcept openai.APIStatusError as e:\n    print(\"Another non-200-range status code was received\")\n    print(e.status_code)\n    print(e.response)\n```\n\nThis code handles different types of errors that might occur while creating a fine-tuning job.\n\n---\n\n## Retries\n\nCertain errors are automatically retried 2 times by default, with a short exponential backoff. Connection errors (for example, due to a network connectivity problem), 408 Request Timeout, 409 Conflict, 429 Rate Limit, and \u003e=500 Internal errors are all retried by default.\n\nYou can use the `max_retries` option to configure or disable retry settings:\n\n```python\nfrom openai import OpenAI\n\nclient = OpenAI(max_retries=0)\n\nclient.with_options(max_retries=5).chat.completions.create(\n    messages=[{\"role\": \"user\", \"content\": \"How can I get the name of the current day in Node.js?\"}],\n    model=\"gpt-3.5-turbo\",\n)\n```\n\n---\n\n **Explanation:**\nSome errors are automatically retried by the library. You can configure how many times to retry or disable retries. It's like trying to reconnect your WiFi if it drops the first time.\n\n**Example:**\n\n```python\nfrom openai import OpenAI\n\nclient = OpenAI(max_retries=0"]},"status":"finished_partial_completion","end_turn":false,"weight":1,"metadata":{"citations":[],"gizmo_id":null,"finish_details":{"type":"max_tokens"},"is_complete":true,"message_type":null,"model_slug":"gpt-4o","default_model_slug":"gpt-4o","pad":"AAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAA","parent_id":"b76e8883-7adc-4e84-8943-fd7180bf9e26","request_id":"8a44a77d7a6f7c6f-EWR","timestamp_":"absolute","shared_conversation_id":"85a63d94-b5d2-49c5-9cda-c84a620e2da7"},"recipient":"all"},"parent":"b76e8883-7adc-4e84-8943-fd7180bf9e26","children":["8b6131c8-61db-4cc5-9d57-148b77fbf8ef"]},{"id":"8b6131c8-61db-4cc5-9d57-148b77fbf8ef","message":{"id":"8b6131c8-61db-4cc5-9d57-148b77fbf8ef","author":{"role":"assistant","metadata":{}},"create_time":1721161038.989432,"content":{"content_type":"text","parts":[")\n\nclient.with_options(max_retries=5).chat.completions.create(\n    messages=[{\"role\": \"user\", \"content\": \"How can I get the name of the current day in Node.js?\"}],\n    model=\"gpt-3.5-turbo\",\n)\n```\n\nThis code configures the client to retry requests up to 5 times.\n\n---\n\n## Timeouts\n\nBy default requests time out after 10 minutes. You can configure this with a `timeout` option, which accepts a float or an [httpx.Timeout](https://www.python-httpx.org/advanced/#fine-tuning-the-configuration) object:\n\n```python\nfrom openai import OpenAI\n\nclient = OpenAI(timeout=20.0)\n\nclient.with_options(timeout=5.0).chat.completions.create(\n    messages=[{\"role\": \"user\", \"content\": \"How can I list all files in a directory using Python?\"}],\n    model=\"gpt-3.5-turbo\",\n)\n```\n\nOn timeout, an `APITimeoutError` is thrown.\n\n---\n\n **Explanation:**\nYou can set how long to wait for a response before timing out. It's like setting a timer for how long you'll wait for a friend before leaving.\n\n**Example:**\n\n```python\nfrom openai import OpenAI\n\nclient = OpenAI(timeout=20.0)\n\nclient.with_options(timeout=5.0).chat.completions.create(\n    messages=[{\"role\": \"user\", \"content\": \"How can I list all files in a directory using Python?\"}],\n    model=\"gpt-3.5-turbo\",\n)\n```\n\nThis code sets a timeout of 20 seconds for all requests, and 5 seconds for a specific request.\n\n---\n\n## Advanced\n\n### Logging\n\nYou can enable logging to see more details about what the library is doing.\n\n```shell\n$ export OPENAI_LOG=debug\n```\n\n---\n\n **Explanation:**\nYou can enable logging to see more details about what the library is doing. It's like turning on a GPS tracker to see where you've been.\n\n**Example:**\n\n```shell\n$ export OPENAI_LOG=debug\n```\n\nThis command enables debug logging.\n\n---\n\n### Making Custom/Undocumented Requests\n\nYou can make requests to undocumented endpoints, params, or response properties. The library can still be used.\n\n```py\nimport httpx\n\nresponse = client.post(\n    \"/foo\",\n    cast_to=httpx.Response,\n    body={\"my_param\": True},\n)\n\nprint(response.headers.get(\"x-foo\"))\n```\n\n---\n\n **Explanation:**\nYou can make requests to undocumented endpoints or add extra parameters. It's like asking for something not on the menu at a restaurant, and the chef might still make it for you.\n\n**Example:**\n\n```py\nimport httpx\n\nresponse = client.post(\n    \"/foo\",\n    cast_to=httpx.Response,\n    body={\"my_param\": True},\n)\n\nprint(response.headers.get(\"x-foo\"))\n```\n\nThis code makes a custom request to an undocumented endpoint.\n\n---\n\n### Configuring the HTTP Client\n\nYou can directly override the [httpx client](https://www.python-httpx.org/api/#client) to customize it for your use case, including support for proxies, custom transports, and additional advanced functionality.\n\n```python\nfrom openai import OpenAI, DefaultHttpxClient\n\nclient = OpenAI(\n    base_url=\"http://my.test.server.example.com:8083\",\n    http_client=DefaultHttpxClient(\n        proxies=\"http://my.test.proxy.example.com\",\n        transport=httpx.HTTPTransport(local_address=\"0.0.0.0\"),\n    ),\n)\n```\n\n---\n\n **Explanation:**\nYou can customize the HTTP client used by the library. It's like customizing your car with different features to suit your needs.\n\n**Example:**\n\n```python\nfrom openai import OpenAI, DefaultHttpxClient\n\nclient = OpenAI(\n    base_url=\"http://my.test.server.example.com:8083\",\n    http_client=DefaultHttpxClient(\n        proxies=\"http://my.test.proxy.example.com\",\n        transport=httpx.HTTPTransport(local_address=\"0.0.0.0\"),\n    ),\n)\n```\n\nThis code configures the client to use a proxy and a custom transport.\n\n---\n\n### Managing HTTP Resources\n\nBy default, the library closes underlying HTTP connections whenever the client is [garbage collected](https://docs.python.org/3/reference/datamodel.html#object.__del__). You can manually close the client using the `.close()` method if desired, or with a context manager that closes when exiting.\n\n```python\nclient.close()\n```\n\n---\n\n **Explanation:**\nYou can manually close the client to free up resources. It's like turning off the lights when you leave a room to save energy.\n\n**Example:**\n\n```python\nclient.close()\n```\n\nThis code closes the client.\n\n---\n\n## Microsoft Azure OpenAI\n\nTo use this library with [Azure OpenAI](https://learn.microsoft.com/azure/ai-services/openai/overview), use the `AzureOpenAI` class instead of the `OpenAI` class.\n\n```python\nfrom openai import AzureOpenAI\n\nclient = AzureOpenAI(\n    api_version=\"2023-07-01-preview\",\n    azure_endpoint=\"https://example-endpoint.openai.azure.com\",\n)\n\ncompletion = client.chat.completions.create(\n    model=\"deployment-name\",\n    messages=[{\"role\": \"user\", \"content\": \"How do I output all files in a directory using Python?\"}],\n)\n\nprint(completion.to_json())\n```\n\n---\n\n **Explanation:**\nIf you are using OpenAI through Microsoft Azure, you need to use the AzureOpenAI class. It's like using a different key to unlock a door.\n\n**Example:**\n\n```python\nfrom openai import AzureOpenAI\n\nclient = AzureOpenAI(\n    api_version=\"2023-07-01-preview\",\n    azure_endpoint=\"https://example-endpoint.openai.azure.com\",\n)\n\ncompletion = client.chat.completions.create(\n    model=\"deployment-name\",\n    messages=[{\"role\": \"user\", \"content\": \"How do I output all files in a directory using Python?\"}],\n)\n\nprint(completion.to_json())\n```\n\nThis code configures the client to use Microsoft Azure OpenAI.\n\n---\n\n## Requirements\n\nYou need Python 3.7 or higher to use this library.\n\n**Example:**\nMake sure your Python version is 3.7 or higher by running:\n\n```sh\npython --version\n```\n\n---\n\n **Explanation:**\nYou need Python 3.7 or higher to use this library. It's like needing a specific version of an app to use certain features.\n\n**Example:**\n\n```sh\npython --version\n```\n\nThis command shows the current Python version installed on your system.\n\n---\n\n## Versioning\n\nThis package generally follows [SemVer](https://semver.org/spec/v2.0.0.html) conventions, though certain backwards-incompatible changes may be released as minor versions:\n\n1. Changes that only affect static types, without breaking runtime behavior.\n2. Changes to library internals which are technically public but not intended or documented for external use. _(Please open a GitHub issue to let us know if you are relying on such internals)_.\n3. Changes that we do not expect to impact the vast majority of users in practice.\n\nWe take backwards-compatibility seriously and work hard to ensure you can rely on a smooth upgrade experience.\n\nWe are keen for your feedback; please open an [issue](https://www.github.com/openai/openai-python/issues) with questions, bugs, or suggestions.\n\n---\n\n **Explanation:**\nThe library follows versioning rules to ensure backward compatibility. The [library](#library) includes type definitions for all request [params](#parameters) and response fields, and offers both synchronous and [asynchronous](#asynchronous) clients powered by [httpx](#http).\n\nIt is generated from our [OpenAPI](#api) specification with [Stainless](#stainless).\n\n---\n\n **Explanation:**\nThe [OpenAI](#api) Python library is like a toolbox that makes it easy to use OpenAI's [AI models](#openais-ai-models) in your [Python](#python) programs. For example, `import openai` connects your script to the library for commands and instructions.\n\n---\n\n## Usage\n\nThe full [API](#api) of this [library](#library) can be found in [api.md](api.md).\n\n```python\nimport os\nfrom openai import OpenAI\n\nclient = OpenAI(\n    api_key=os.environ.get(\"OPENAI_API_KEY\"),\n)\n\nchat_completion = client.chat.completions.create(\n    messages=[\n        {\n            \"role\": \"user\",\n            \"content\": \"Say this is a test\",\n        }\n    ],\n    model=\"gpt-3.5-turbo\",\n)\n```\n\n---\n\n **Explanation:**\nHere's how you use the [library](#library) to talk to the [AI models](#openais-ai-models). Think of this like having a conversation with your smart robot assistant. You set up the connection, ask it to say something, and then it responds.\n\n**Example:**\n\n```python\nimport os\nfrom openai import OpenAI\n\nclient = OpenAI(api_key=os.environ.get(\"OPENAI_API_KEY\"))\n\nchat_completion = client.chat.completions.create(\n    model=\"gpt-3.5-turbo\",\n    messages=[{\"role\": \"user\", \"content\": \"Say this is a test\"}],\n)\n\nprint(chat_completion.choices[0].message.content)\n```\n\nThis code sets up the [AI](#openais-ai-models) client and asks it to say \"This is a test.\"\n\n---\n\n## Polling Helpers\n\nWhen interacting with the [API](#api), some actions such as starting a Run and adding files to vector stores are [asynchronous](#asynchronous) and take time to complete. The [SDK](#sdk) includes helper functions which will poll the status until it reaches a terminal state and then return the resulting object. If an [API](#api) method results in an action that could benefit from polling there will be a corresponding version of the method ending in '_and_poll'.\n\nFor instance, to create a Run and poll until it reaches a terminal state, you can run:\n\n```python\nrun = client.beta.threads.runs.create_and_poll(\n    thread_id=thread.id,\n    assistant_id=assistant.id,\n)\n```\n\n---\n\n **Explanation:**\nSome actions take time to complete, like starting a process or uploading files. Polling helpers keep checking until these actions are done. Imagine you are baking a cake and you keep checking the oven until the cake is ready.\n\n**Example:**\n\n```python\nrun = client.beta.threads.runs.create_and_poll(\n    thread_id=thread.id,\n    assistant_id=assistant.id,\n)\n```\n\nThis code starts a process and waits until it's finished.\n\n---\n\n## Bulk Upload Helpers\n\nWhen creating and interacting with vector stores, you can use polling helpers to monitor the status of operations. For convenience, we also provide a bulk upload helper to allow you to simultaneously upload several files at once.\n\n```python\nsample_files = [Path(\"sample-paper.pdf\"), ...]\n\nbatch = await client.vector_stores.file_batches.upload_and_poll(\n    store.id,\n    files=sample_files,\n)\n```\n\n---\n\n **Explanation:**\nYou can upload multiple files at once and check their status. This is like sending a bunch of letters at the post office and waiting to see when they are all delivered.\n\n**Example:**\n\n```python\nfrom pathlib import Path\n\nsample_files = [Path(\"sample-paper.pdf\"), ...]\n\nbatch = await client.vector_stores.file_batches.upload_and_poll(\n    store.id,\n    files=sample_files,\n)\n```\n\nThis code uploads several files and waits until they're all done.\n\n---\n\n## Streaming Helpers\n\nThe [SDK](#sdk) also includes helpers to process streams and handle incoming events.\n\n```python\nwith client.beta.threads.runs.stream(\n    thread_id=thread.id,\n    assistant_id=assistant.id,\n    instructions=\"Please address the user as Jane Doe. The user has a premium account.\",\n) as stream:\n    for event in stream:\n        if event.type == \"thread.message.delta\" and event.data.delta.content:\n            print(event.data.delta.content[0].text)\n```\n\n---\n\n **Explanation:**\nYou can stream responses from the [AI](#openais-ai-models), which means you get parts of the response as they come in, instead of waiting for the whole thing. It's like watching a YouTube video as it loads rather than waiting for the entire video to download first.\n\n**Example:**\n\n```python\nwith client.beta.threads.runs.stream(\n    thread_id=thread.id,\n    assistant_id=assistant.id,\n    instructions=\"Please address the user as Jane Doe. The user has a premium account.\",\n) as stream:\n    for event in stream:\n        if event.type == \"thread.message.delta\" and event.data.delta.content:\n            print(event.data.delta.content[0].text)\n```\n\nThis code streams the response from the [AI](#openais-ai-models) and prints it piece by piece.\n\n---\n\n## Async Usage\n\nSimply import `AsyncOpenAI` instead of `OpenAI` and use `await` with each [API](#api) call:\n\n```python\nimport os\nimport asyncio\nfrom openai import AsyncOpenAI\n\nclient = AsyncOpenAI(\n    api_key=os.environ.get(\"OPENAI_API_KEY\"),\n)\n\nasync def main() -\u003e None:\n    chat_completion = await client.chat.completions.create(\n        messages=[\n            {\n                \"role\": \"user\",\n                \"content\": \"Say this is a test\",\n            }\n        ],\n        model=\"gpt-3.5-turbo\",\n    )\n\nasyncio.run(main())\n```\n\nFunctionality between the synchronous and [asynchronous](#asynchronous)"]},"status":"finished_partial_completion","end_turn":false,"weight":1,"metadata":{"citations":[],"gizmo_id":null,"finish_details":{"type":"max_tokens"},"is_complete":true,"message_type":null,"model_slug":"gpt-4o","default_model_slug":"gpt-4o","pad":"AAAAAAAAAAAAAAAA","parent_id":"aaa29c9e-43d8-4209-a8c9-088294e2e83e","request_id":"8a44b85c1aab4217-EWR","timestamp_":"absolute","shared_conversation_id":"85a63d94-b5d2-49c5-9cda-c84a620e2da7"},"recipient":"all"},"parent":"aaa29c9e-43d8-4209-a8c9-088294e2e83e","children":["b5601b2a-fa8d-43af-9150-fc98d1dfb9df"]},{"id":"b5601b2a-fa8d-43af-9150-fc98d1dfb9df","message":{"id":"b5601b2a-fa8d-43af-9150-fc98d1dfb9df","author":{"role":"assistant","metadata":{}},"create_time":1721161696.519707,"content":{"content_type":"text","parts":[" clients is otherwise identical.\n\n---\n\n **Explanation:**\nYou can use the [library](#library) with [asynchronous](#asynchronous) code, which lets your program do other things while waiting for the [AI](#openais-ai-models) to respond. It's like cooking several dishes at once instead of one after the other.\n\n**Example:**\n\n```python\nimport os\nimport asyncio\nfrom openai import AsyncOpenAI\n\nclient = AsyncOpenAI(api_key=os.environ.get(\"OPENAI_API_KEY\"))\n\nasync def main() -\u003e None:\n    chat_completion = await client.chat.completions.create(\n        model=\"gpt-3.5-turbo\",\n        messages=[{\"role\": \"user\", \"content\": \"Say this is a test\"}],\n    )\n\nasyncio.run(main())\n```\n\nThis code does the same thing as before but in an [asynchronous](#asynchronous) way.\n\n---\n\n## Streaming Responses\n\nWe provide support for streaming responses using Server Side Events (SSE).\n\n```python\nfrom openai import OpenAI\n\nclient = OpenAI()\n\nstream = client.chat.completions.create(\n    model=\"gpt-4\",\n    messages=[{\"role\": \"user\", \"content\": \"Say this is a test\"}],\n    stream=True,\n)\nfor chunk in stream:\n    print(chunk.choices[0].delta.content or \"\", end=\"\")\n```\n\nThe async client uses the exact same interface.\n\n```python\nfrom openai import AsyncOpenAI\n\nclient = AsyncOpenAI()\n\nasync def main():\n    stream = await client.chat.completions.create(\n        model=\"gpt-4\",\n        messages=[{\"role\": \"user\", \"content\": \"Say this is a test\"}],\n        stream=True,\n    )\n    async for chunk in stream:\n        print(chunk.choices[0].delta.content or \"\", end=\"\")\n\nasyncio.run(main())\n```\n\n---\n\n **Explanation:**\nYou can handle streaming responses from the [AI](#openais-ai-models) in both synchronous and [asynchronous](#asynchronous) ways. It's like watching a live broadcast or listening to live radio where the content comes in chunks.\n\n**Example:**\n\n```python\nfrom openai import OpenAI\n\nclient = OpenAI()\n\nstream = client.chat.completions.create(\n    model=\"gpt-4\",\n    messages=[{\"role\": \"user\", \"content\": \"Say this is a test\"}],\n    stream=True,\n)\nfor chunk in stream:\n    print(chunk.choices[0].delta.content or \"\", end=\"\")\n```\n\nThis code streams the response from the [AI](#openais-ai-models) and prints it as it comes.\n\n---\n\n## Module-Level Client\n\nYou can set up a global client instance, which is useful for quick experiments but not recommended for complex applications.\n\n```py\nimport openai\n\nopenai.api_key = 'your-api-key'\n\ncompletion = openai.chat.completions.create(\n    model=\"gpt-4\",\n    messages=[{\"role\": \"user\", \"content\": \"How do I output all files in a directory using Python?\"}],\n)\n\nprint(completion.choices[0].message.content)\n```\n\n---\n\n **Explanation:**\nYou can set up a global client instance, which is useful for quick experiments but not recommended for complex applications. It's like having a universal remote that works for all your devices, but it might not have all the features you need for each specific device.\n\n**Example:**\n\n```python\nimport openai\n\nopenai.api_key = 'your-api-key'\n\ncompletion = openai.chat.completions.create(\n    model=\"gpt-4\",\n    messages=[{\"role\": \"user\", \"content\": \"How do I output all files in a directory using Python?\"}],\n)\n\nprint(completion.choices[0].message.content)\n```\n\nThis code uses a global client to get a response from the [AI](#openais-ai-models).\n\n---\n\n## Using Types\n\nThe [library](#library) uses typed requests and responses, which means it can help you catch mistakes while you write your code.\n\n```python\nfrom openai import OpenAI\n\nclient = OpenAI()\n\ncompletion = client.chat.completions.create(\n    messages=[{\"role\": \"user\", \"content\": \"Can you generate an example json object describing a fruit?\"}],\n    model=\"gpt-3.5-turbo-1106\",\n    response_format={\"type\": \"json_object\"},\n)\n```\n\n---\n\n **Explanation:**\nThe [library](#library) uses typed requests and responses, which means it can help you catch mistakes while you write your code. Think of it as having a spell-checker for your programming instructions.\n\n**Example:**\n\n```python\nfrom openai import OpenAI\n\nclient = OpenAI()\n\ncompletion = client.chat.completions.create(\n    messages=[{\"role\": \"user\", \"content\": \"Can you generate an example json object describing a fruit?\"}],\n    model=\"gpt-3.5-turbo-1106\",\n    response_format={\"type\": \"json_object\"},\n)\n```\n\nThis code asks the [AI](#openais-ai-models) to generate a JSON object describing a fruit.\n\n---\n\n## Pagination\n\nSome [API](#api) responses are too large to send all at once, so they are split into pages. The [library](#library) can automatically handle fetching these pages for you.\n\n```python\nimport openai\n\nclient = OpenAI()\n\nall_jobs = []\nfor job in client.fine_tuning.jobs.list(limit=20):\n    all_jobs.append(job)\n\nprint(all_jobs)\n```\n\n---\n\n **Explanation:**\nSome [API](#api) responses are too large to send all at once, so they are split into pages. The [library](#library) can automatically handle fetching these pages for you. It's like getting a long book in several smaller, manageable volumes instead of one big, heavy book.\n\n**Example:**\n\n```python\nimport openai\n\nclient = OpenAI()\n\nall_jobs = []\nfor job in client.fine_tuning.jobs.list(limit=20):\n    all_jobs.append(job)\n\nprint(all_jobs)\n```\n\nThis code fetches all jobs, automatically handling multiple pages of results.\n\n---\n\n## Nested Params\n\nSome [parameters](#parameters) are nested dictionaries. You can pass them as dictionaries in your requests.\n\n```python\nfrom openai import OpenAI\n\nclient = OpenAI()\n\ncompletion = client.chat.completions.create(\n    messages=[{\"role\": \"user\", \"content\": \"Can you generate an example json object describing a fruit?\"}],\n    model=\"gpt-3.5-turbo-1106\",\n    response_format={\"type\": \"json_object\"},\n)\n```\n\n---\n\n **Explanation:**\nSome [parameters](#parameters) are nested dictionaries. You can pass them as dictionaries in your requests. It's like having a folder inside another folder on your computer.\n\n**Example:**\n\n```python\nfrom openai import OpenAI\n\nclient = OpenAI()\n\ncompletion = client.chat.completions.create(\n    messages=[{\"role\": \"user\", \"content\": \"Can you generate an example json object describing a fruit?\"}],\n    model=\"gpt-3.5-turbo-1106\",\n    response_format={\"type\": \"json_object\"},\n)\n```\n\nThis code asks the [AI](#openais-ai-models) to generate a JSON object.\n\n---\n\n## File Uploads\n\nYou can upload files directly to the [API](#api), which can be used for things like fine-tuning models.\n\n```python\nfrom pathlib import Path\nfrom openai import OpenAI\n\nclient = OpenAI()\n\nclient.files.create(\n    file=Path(\"input.jsonl\"),\n    purpose=\"fine-tune\",\n)\n```\n\n---\n\n **Explanation:**\nYou can upload files directly to the [API](#api), which can be used for things like fine-tuning models. It's like uploading a document to a website so that the site can use the information in the document.\n\n**Example:**\n\n```python\nfrom pathlib import Path\nfrom openai import OpenAI\n\nclient = OpenAI()\n\nclient.files.create(\n    file=Path(\"input.jsonl\"),\n    purpose=\"fine-tune\",\n)\n```\n\nThis code uploads a file for fine-tuning a model.\n\n---\n\n## Handling Errors\n\nThe [library](#library) provides error handling for different types of errors that can occur while interacting with the [API](#api).\n\n```python\nimport openai\nfrom openai import OpenAI\n\nclient = OpenAI()\n\ntry:\n    client.fine_tuning.jobs.create(\n        model=\"gpt-3.5-turbo\",\n        training_file=\"file-abc123\",\n    )\nexcept openai.APIConnectionError as e:\n    print(\"The server could not be reached\")\n    print(e.__cause__)\nexcept openai.RateLimitError as e:\n    print(\"A 429 status code was received; we should back off a bit.\")\nexcept openai.APIStatusError as e:\n    print(\"Another non-200-range status code was received\")\n    print(e.status_code)\n    print(e.response)\n```\n\n---\n\n **Explanation:**\nThe [library](#library) provides error handling for different types of errors that can occur while interacting with the [API](#api). It's like having a plan for what to do if something goes wrong while you're working on a project.\n\n**Example:**\n\n```python\nimport openai\nfrom openai import OpenAI\n\nclient = OpenAI()\n\ntry:\n    client.fine_tuning.jobs.create(\n        model=\"gpt-3.5-turbo\",\n        training_file=\"file-abc123\",\n    )\nexcept openai.APIConnectionError as e:\n    print(\"The server could not be reached\")\n    print(e.__cause__)\nexcept openai.RateLimitError as e:\n    print(\"A 429 status code"]},"status":"finished_partial_completion","end_turn":false,"weight":1,"metadata":{"citations":[],"gizmo_id":null,"finish_details":{"type":"max_tokens"},"is_complete":true,"message_type":null,"model_slug":"gpt-4o","default_model_slug":"gpt-4o","pad":"AA","parent_id":"1c95eb79-84f5-4c73-bb20-98fac5932478","request_id":"8a44bb896c7e4217-EWR","timestamp_":"absolute","shared_conversation_id":"85a63d94-b5d2-49c5-9cda-c84a620e2da7"},"recipient":"all"},"parent":"1c95eb79-84f5-4c73-bb20-98fac5932478","children":["ea3f626e-4949-451b-8750-5284ccc6c913"]},{"id":"ea3f626e-4949-451b-8750-5284ccc6c913","message":{"id":"ea3f626e-4949-451b-8750-5284ccc6c913","author":{"role":"assistant","metadata":{}},"create_time":1721161774.00827,"content":{"content_type":"text","parts":[" was received; we should back off a bit.\")\nexcept openai.APIStatusError as e:\n    print(\"Another non-200-range status code was received\")\n    print(e.status_code)\n    print(e.response)\n```\n\nThis code handles different types of errors that might occur while creating a fine-tuning job.\n\n---\n\n## Retries\n\nCertain errors are automatically retried 2 times by default, with a short exponential backoff. Connection errors (for example, due to a network connectivity problem), 408 Request Timeout, 409 Conflict, 429 Rate Limit, and \u003e=500 Internal errors are all retried by default.\n\nYou can use the `max_retries` option to configure or disable retry settings:\n\n```python\nfrom openai import OpenAI\n\nclient = OpenAI(max_retries=0)\n\nclient.with_options(max_retries=5).chat.completions.create(\n    messages=[{\"role\": \"user\", \"content\": \"How can I get the name of the current day in Node.js?\"}],\n    model=\"gpt-3.5-turbo\",\n)\n```\n\n---\n\n **Explanation:**\nSome errors are automatically retried by the [library](#library). You can configure how many times to retry or disable retries. It's like trying to reconnect your WiFi if it drops the first time.\n\n**Example:**\n\n```python\nfrom openai import OpenAI\n\nclient = OpenAI(max_retries=0)\n\nclient.with_options(max_retries=5).chat.completions.create(\n    messages=[{\"role\": \"user\", \"content\": \"How can I get the name of the current day in Node.js?\"}],\n    model=\"gpt-3.5-turbo\",\n)\n```\n\nThis code configures the client to retry requests up to 5 times.\n\n---\n\n## Timeouts\n\nBy default, requests time out after 10 minutes. You can configure this with a `timeout` option, which accepts a float or an [httpx.Timeout](https://www.python-httpx.org/advanced/#fine-tuning-the-configuration) object:\n\n```python\nfrom openai import OpenAI\n\nclient = OpenAI(timeout=20.0)\n\nclient.with_options(timeout=5.0).chat.completions.create(\n    messages=[{\"role\": \"user\", \"content\": \"How can I list all files in a directory using Python?\"}],\n    model=\"gpt-3.5-turbo\",\n)\n```\n\nOn timeout, an `APITimeoutError` is thrown.\n\n---\n\n **Explanation:**\nYou can set how long to wait for a response before timing out. It's like setting a timer for how long you'll wait for a friend before leaving.\n\n**Example:**\n\n```python\nfrom openai import OpenAI\n\nclient = OpenAI(timeout=20.0)\n\nclient.with_options(timeout=5.0).chat.completions.create(\n    messages=[{\"role\": \"user\", \"content\": \"How can I list all files in a directory using Python?\"}],\n    model=\"gpt-3.5-turbo\",\n)\n```\n\nThis code sets a timeout of 20 seconds for all requests, and 5 seconds for a specific request.\n\n---\n\n## Advanced\n\n### Logging\n\nYou can enable logging to see more details about what the [library](#library) is doing.\n\n```shell\n$ export OPENAI_LOG=debug\n```\n\n---\n\n **Explanation:**\nYou can enable logging to see more details about what the [library](#library) is doing. It's like turning on a GPS tracker to see where you've been.\n\n**Example:**\n\n```shell\n$ export OPENAI_LOG=debug\n```\n\nThis command enables debug logging.\n\n---\n\n### Making Custom/Undocumented Requests\n\nYou can make requests to undocumented endpoints, params, or response properties. The [library](#library) can still be used.\n\n```py\nimport httpx\n\nresponse = client.post(\n    \"/foo\",\n    cast_to=httpx.Response,\n    body={\"my_param\": True},\n)\n\nprint(response.headers.get(\"x-foo\"))\n```\n\n---\n\n **Explanation:**\nYou can make requests to undocumented endpoints or add extra parameters. It's like asking for something not on the menu at a restaurant, and the chef might still make it for you.\n\n**Example:**\n\n```py\nimport httpx\n\nresponse = client.post(\n    \"/foo\",\n    cast_to=httpx.Response,\n    body={\"my_param\": True},\n)\n\nprint(response.headers.get(\"x-foo\"))\n```\n\nThis code makes a custom request to an undocumented endpoint.\n\n---\n\n### Configuring the HTTP Client\n\nYou can directly override the [httpx client](https://www.python-httpx.org/api/#client) to customize it for your use case, including support for proxies, custom transports, and additional advanced functionality.\n\n```python\nfrom openai import OpenAI, DefaultHttpxClient\n\nclient = OpenAI(\n    base_url=\"http://my.test.server.example.com:8083\",\n    http_client=DefaultHttpxClient(\n        proxies=\"http://my.test.proxy.example.com\",\n        transport=httpx.HTTPTransport(local_address=\"0.0.0.0\"),\n    ),\n)\n```\n\n---\n\n **Explanation:**\nYou can customize the HTTP client used by the [library](#library). It's like customizing your car with different features to suit your needs.\n\n**Example:**\n\n```python\nfrom openai import OpenAI, DefaultHttpxClient\n\nclient = OpenAI(\n    base_url=\"http://my.test.server.example.com:8083\",\n    http_client=DefaultHttpxClient(\n        proxies=\"http://my.test.proxy.example.com\",\n        transport=httpx.HTTPTransport(local_address=\"0.0.0.0\"),\n    ),\n)\n```\n\nThis code configures the client to use a proxy and a custom transport.\n\n---\n\n### Managing HTTP Resources\n\nBy default, the [library](#library) closes underlying HTTP connections whenever the client is [garbage collected](https://docs.python.org/3/reference/datamodel.html#object.__del__). You can manually close the client using the `.close()` method if desired, or with a context manager that closes when exiting.\n\n```python\nclient.close()\n```\n\n---\n\n **Explanation:**\nYou can manually close the client to free up resources. It's like turning off the lights when you leave a room to save energy.\n\n**Example:**\n\n```python\nclient.close()\n```\n\nThis code closes the client.\n\n---\n\n## Microsoft Azure OpenAI\n\nTo use this [library](#library) with [Azure OpenAI](https://learn.microsoft.com/azure/ai-services/openai/overview), use the `AzureOpenAI` class instead of the `OpenAI` class.\n\n```python\nfrom openai import AzureOpenAI\n\nclient = AzureOpenAI(\n    api_version=\"2023-07-01-preview\",\n    azure_endpoint=\"https://example-endpoint.openai.azure.com\",\n)\n\ncompletion = client.chat.completions.create(\n    model=\"deployment-name\",\n    messages=[{\"role\": \"user\", \"content\": \"How do I output all files in a directory using Python?\"}],\n)\n\nprint(completion.to_json())\n```\n\n---\n\n **Explanation:**\nIf you are using OpenAI through Microsoft Azure, you need to use the AzureOpenAI class. It's like using a different key to unlock a door.\n\n**Example:**\n\n```python\nfrom openai import AzureOpenAI\n\nclient = AzureOpenAI(\n    api_version=\"2023-07-01-preview\",\n    azure_endpoint=\"https://example-endpoint.openai.azure.com\",\n)\n\ncompletion = client.chat.completions.create(\n    model=\"deployment-name\",\n    messages=[{\"role\": \"user\", \"content\": \"How do I output all files in a directory using Python?\"}],\n)\n\nprint(completion.to_json())\n```\n\nThis code configures the client to use Microsoft Azure OpenAI.\n\n---\n\n## Requirements\n\nYou need [Python](#python) 3.7 or higher to use this [library](#library).\n\n**Example:**\nMake sure your [Python](#python) version is 3.7 or higher by running:\n\n```sh\npython --version\n```\n\n---\n\n **Explanation:**\nYou need [Python](#python) 3.7 or higher to use this [library](#library). It's like needing a specific version of an app to use certain features.\n\n**Example:**\n\n```sh\npython --version\n```\n\nThis command shows the current [Python](#python) version installed on your system.\n\n---\n\n## Versioning\n\nThis package generally follows [SemVer](https://semver.org/spec/v2.0.0.html) conventions, though certain backwards-incompatible changes may be released as minor versions:\n\n1. Changes that only affect static types, without breaking runtime behavior.\n2. Changes to library internals which are technically public but not intended or documented for external use. _(Please open a GitHub issue to let us know if you are relying on such internals)_.\n3. Changes that we do not expect to impact the vast majority of users in practice.\n\nWe take backwards-compatibility seriously and work hard to ensure you can rely on a smooth upgrade experience.\n\nWe are keen for your feedback; please open an [issue](https://www.github.com/openai/openai-python/issues) with questions, bugs, or suggestions.\n\n---\n\n **Explanation:**\nThe [library](#library) follows versioning rules to ensure backward compatibility. It's like updating an app on your phone to get new features without breaking the old ones.\n\n**Example:**\n\n```sh\npip install openai==1.0.0\n```\n\nThis command installs a specific version of the OpenAI [library](#library).\n\n---\n\nI have revised the README.md to ensure every technical term is properly linked and explained. import os from openai import OpenAI client = OpenAI( # This is the default and can be omitted api_key=os.environ.get("OPENAI_API_KEY"), ) chat_completion = client.chat.completions.create( messages=[ { "role": "user", "content": "Say this is a test", } ], model="gpt-3.5-turbo", ) What does this code do and what will it do?

This Python code snippet is designed to interact with OpenAI's GPT-3.5 API to generate a chat completion (i.e., a response from the AI) based on a given prompt. Let's break down what each part of the code does:

1. **Importing Modules:**

   <pre><div class="dark bg-gray-950 rounded-md border-[0.5px] border-token-border-medium"><div class="flex items-center relative text-token-text-secondary bg-token-main-surface-secondary px-4 py-2 text-xs font-sans justify-between rounded-t-md"><span>python</span><div class="flex items-center"><span class="" data-state="closed"><button class="flex gap-1 items-center"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="24" height="24" fill="none" viewBox="0 0 24 24" class="icon-sm"><path fill="currentColor" fill-rule="evenodd" d="M7 5a3 3 0 0 1 3-3h9a3 3 0 0 1 3 3v9a3 3 0 0 1-3 3h-2v2a3 3 0 0 1-3 3H5a3 3 0 0 1-3-3v-9a3 3 0 0 1 3-3h2zm2 2h5a3 3 0 0 1 3 3v5h2a1 1 0 0 0 1-1V5a1 1 0 0 0-1-1h-9a1 1 0 0 0-1 1zM5 9a1 1 0 0 0-1 1v9a1 1 0 0 0 1 1h9a1 1 0 0 0 1-1v-9a1 1 0 0 0-1-1z" clip-rule="evenodd"></path></svg>Copy code</button></span></div></div><div class="overflow-y-auto p-4" dir="ltr"><code class="!whitespace-pre hljs language-python">import os
   from openai import OpenAI
   </code></div></div></pre>

   This imports the** **`os` module, which allows you to interact with the operating system, and the** **`OpenAI` module from the** **`openai` package, which provides the tools to interact with OpenAI's API.
2. **Creating an OpenAI Client:**

   <pre><div class="dark bg-gray-950 rounded-md border-[0.5px] border-token-border-medium"><div class="flex items-center relative text-token-text-secondary bg-token-main-surface-secondary px-4 py-2 text-xs font-sans justify-between rounded-t-md"><span>python</span><div class="flex items-center"><span class="" data-state="closed"><button class="flex gap-1 items-center"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="24" height="24" fill="none" viewBox="0 0 24 24" class="icon-sm"><path fill="currentColor" fill-rule="evenodd" d="M7 5a3 3 0 0 1 3-3h9a3 3 0 0 1 3 3v9a3 3 0 0 1-3 3h-2v2a3 3 0 0 1-3 3H5a3 3 0 0 1-3-3v-9a3 3 0 0 1 3-3h2zm2 2h5a3 3 0 0 1 3 3v5h2a1 1 0 0 0 1-1V5a1 1 0 0 0-1-1h-9a1 1 0 0 0-1 1zM5 9a1 1 0 0 0-1 1v9a1 1 0 0 0 1 1h9a1 1 0 0 0 1-1v-9a1 1 0 0 0-1-1z" clip-rule="evenodd"></path></svg>Copy code</button></span></div></div><div class="overflow-y-auto p-4" dir="ltr"><code class="!whitespace-pre hljs language-python">client = OpenAI(
       api_key=os.environ.get("OPENAI_API_KEY"),
   )
   </code></div></div></pre>

   This creates an instance of the** **`OpenAI` client. The** **`api_key` is fetched from the environment variable** **`OPENAI_API_KEY`. This key is essential for authenticating and authorizing requests to OpenAI's API.
3. **Generating a Chat Completion:**

   <pre><div class="dark bg-gray-950 rounded-md border-[0.5px] border-token-border-medium"><div class="flex items-center relative text-token-text-secondary bg-token-main-surface-secondary px-4 py-2 text-xs font-sans justify-between rounded-t-md"><span>python</span><div class="flex items-center"><span class="" data-state="closed"><button class="flex gap-1 items-center"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="24" height="24" fill="none" viewBox="0 0 24 24" class="icon-sm"><path fill="currentColor" fill-rule="evenodd" d="M7 5a3 3 0 0 1 3-3h9a3 3 0 0 1 3 3v9a3 3 0 0 1-3 3h-2v2a3 3 0 0 1-3 3H5a3 3 0 0 1-3-3v-9a3 3 0 0 1 3-3h2zm2 2h5a3 3 0 0 1 3 3v5h2a1 1 0 0 0 1-1V5a1 1 0 0 0-1-1h-9a1 1 0 0 0-1 1zM5 9a1 1 0 0 0-1 1v9a1 1 0 0 0 1 1h9a1 1 0 0 0 1-1v-9a1 1 0 0 0-1-1z" clip-rule="evenodd"></path></svg>Copy code</button></span></div></div><div class="overflow-y-auto p-4" dir="ltr"><code class="!whitespace-pre hljs language-python">chat_completion = client.chat.completions.create(
       messages=[
           {
               "role": "user",
               "content": "Say this is a test",
           }
       ],
       model="gpt-3.5-turbo",
   )
   </code></div></div></pre>

   This block sends a request to the OpenAI API to create a chat completion. The** **`messages` parameter is a list of dictionaries, each representing a message in the conversation. In this case, there's one message with the role** **`"user"` and the content** **`"Say this is a test"`. The** **`model` parameter specifies which version of the language model to use, in this case,** **`"gpt-3.5-turbo"`.

### What the Code Will Do:

1. **Retrieve the API Key:** The code retrieves the OpenAI API key from the environment variables. This key must be set in your system's environment for the code to work. If the key is not set,** **`os.environ.get("OPENAI_API_KEY")` will return** **`None`.
2. **Create a Client Instance:** Using the retrieved API key, the code creates an instance of the OpenAI client, which will be used to make requests to the API.
3. **Send a Chat Request:** The code sends a request to the OpenAI API to generate a response based on the prompt "Say this is a test". The API processes this request and generates a response using the specified model,** **`"gpt-3.5-turbo"`.

### Expected Outcome:

The response from the OpenAI API will be an object containing the generated completion. This completion will include a message from the AI with content that responds to the user's prompt. Since the prompt is "Say this is a test", the AI's response might be something like "This is a test".

In this output:

* `usage` provides information about the number of tokens used in the request and response.

chat_completion = openai.ChatCompletion.create(

)

To print out the response from the chat completion, you need to access the** **`choices` attribute of the** **`chat_completion`object. Here's the modified script:

### Modified Script to Print the Response:

<pre><div class="dark bg-gray-950 rounded-md border-[0.5px] border-token-border-medium"><div class="flex items-center relative text-token-text-secondary bg-token-main-surface-secondary px-4 py-2 text-xs font-sans justify-between rounded-t-md"><span>python</span><div class="flex items-center"><span class="" data-state="closed"><button class="flex gap-1 items-center"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="24" height="24" fill="none" viewBox="0 0 24 24" class="icon-sm"><path fill="currentColor" fill-rule="evenodd" d="M7 5a3 3 0 0 1 3-3h9a3 3 0 0 1 3 3v9a3 3 0 0 1-3 3h-2v2a3 3 0 0 1-3 3H5a3 3 0 0 1-3-3v-9a3 3 0 0 1 3-3h2zm2 2h5a3 3 0 0 1 3 3v5h2a1 1 0 0 0 1-1V5a1 1 0 0 0-1-1h-9a1 1 0 0 0-1 1zM5 9a1 1 0 0 0-1 1v9a1 1 0 0 0 1 1h9a1 1 0 0 0 1-1v-9a1 1 0 0 0-1-1z" clip-rule="evenodd"></path></svg>Copy code</button></span></div></div><div class="overflow-y-auto p-4" dir="ltr"><code class="!whitespace-pre hljs language-python">import os
from openai import OpenAI

# Fetch the API key from environment variables
api_key = os.environ.get("OPENAI_API_KEY")

# Check if the API key is present
if not api_key:
    raise ValueError("API key is missing. Please set the OPENAI_API_KEY environment variable.")

# Create an OpenAI client
client = OpenAI(api_key=api_key)

# Generate a chat completion
chat_completion = client.chat.completions.create(
    model="gpt-3.5-turbo",
    messages=[
        {
            "role": "user",
            "content": "Say this is a test",
        }
    ],
)

# Print the output
print(chat_completion['choices'][0]['message']['content'])
</code></div></div></pre>

### Explanation:

1. **API Key Check:** The script ensures that the** **`OPENAI_API_KEY` environment variable is set.
2. **Creating OpenAI Client:** The** **`OpenAI` client is instantiated with the provided API key.
3. **Generating Chat Completion:** The** **`client.chat.completions.create` method is called with the model and message parameters to generate a chat completion.
4. **Printing the Response:** The response from the chat completion is accessed via** **`chat_completion['choices'][0]['message']['content']` and printed.

### Running the Script:

# Check if the API key is present
if not api_key:
    raise ValueError("API key is missing. Please set the OPENAI_API_KEY environment variable.")

# Set the API key
openai.api_key = api_key

# Generate a chat completion
response = openai.ChatCompletion.create(
    model="gpt-3.5-turbo",
    messages=[
        {"role": "user", "content": "Say this is a test"}
    ]
)

# Print the output
print(response.choices[0].message['content'])
</code></div></div></pre>

3. **Generating Chat Completion:** The** **`openai.ChatCompletion.create` method is used to generate a chat completion.
4. **Printing the Response:** The response object contains the AI's reply. The** **`print(response.choices[0].message['content'])` line extracts and prints the content of the first choice in the response.
